<Rate>1< /Rate><Review>This was my second time here and will probably be the last time I bring anyone here.  Let me just give a recap on what took place the first time and the major difference this time around.

The first time, I went with my co-workers on a Wednesday in November. We had Amy and Travis who were both personable and wonderful to talk to. They were both knowledgeable and they made us felt welcome. Both gave us sufficient time to taste the wine. I was the DD so two of my co-workers drank. We called ahead to ensure we can have a picnic as they do the wine tasting. All was well and my coworker liked the experience so much we ordered a bottle to be split between the two of them. When we left I loved it so much I made sure to remember this place to try again when my family visits.

The second time was a dismal experience or should I say it was a total nightmare. Mind you, we went on a Saturday this time but we kept that in mind and didn't plan to overstay our hour and a half limit. I can't even recall the name of the person we had since it was such a sad experience.

1) When we arrive the person  (Domenico) helping lead us to the yard where the tasting was going to take place. We requested to sit under the Wisteria since we were the first one there and no one else was there. We were literally the first party. Well, that didn't happen because he told us it was reserved. Fine. If it's reserve we can't do much but lo and behold it wasn't at all. The next party of two came in and they requested the table and they received it. First strike. It was a matter of principles at this point.

2) Our party of 4 was seated near the doors. As we sat down I reminded him that only 3 out of the 4 will do the tasting. Something that I mentioned prior when we were filling out paper works. As I was setting up our Charcuterie board he came over and said "Don't focus on that, you should focus on the tasting first. You shouldn't eat anything before tasting."  Mind you, I was not doing a tasting so I should've been free to set this up while my party did the tasting which I told him as he was now rushing us. Second strike. I get it. You drink certain wine with certain food. I'm no pro but that much I understand. The fact that he kept rushing us to taste the wine was a huge no for me. You want to enjoy your experience tasting the wine not chugging it down.

3) It was wine chugging/rushing, not wine tasting as my family later deemed it. After the first wine, he came back and kept trying to get us to try the next one already even before my family finished the first tasting. My husband who greatly enjoyed the wine was by now done with the experience. We were allotted an hour and a half but it felt like he wanted us out 30 minutes in.

4) My husband and mom enjoyed the Maximus so they ordered a bottle but yet again you would think they would let us enjoy the bottle with an hour left. Nope. We basically felt rush to finish it. Which in turn resulting in not enjoying the wine yet again.

Overall the experience was night and day compared to my first time there. I know that it is a Saturday and they are probably booked up but why would they assume we were going to overstay our time or that me setting up our food will deter them off schedule. I am not tasting at all. There are three people who are they weren't helping me set up so why would you rush us.  Safe to say it was a total waste of $130+ for such an experience. I will not be going back and I will definitely not recommend this winery to anyone I know.

Choose a winery that actually wants you to be their guest rather than just another number. Next time I will try a different winery or stick close to home. We live in the Tri-valley and are surrounded by local wineries. I had such a wonderful first experience there I wanted to share it with my family but it was truly disappointing. I felt so awful leaving there.<//Review>< pictures>

< Review>
My wife and our 2 sons visited this winery this past Saturday for tasting.

Before being able to do a tasting, I was asked to sign a lengthy legal liability release document requiring me to "accept sole responsibility for any injury to myself, including, but not limited to, personal injury, illness, disability, death, damage, loss, claim, liability, or expense, of any kind, that I may experience or incur in connection with my visit or participation in wine tasting at Bennett Lane Winery" and further "forfeit all right to bring any and all claims against Bennett Lane Winery for any reason."

<Rating>2</Rating><Text>The place was good but comparing it to other places it could be better. The wine is good for tasting with food, pretty good for a blend and excellent for the price but is not the finest wine.

Other wineries focused on talking about their soil (terroir), their history and the quality of the harvest and they abstained from describing the wine. I like this because it lets you have your own non-influenced tasting experience with the wine while knowing how it was made. In Bennett Lane they talked about what the critics have said about them and they also described the flavors of the wine. This could be nice for people learning how to taste wine but it could be better if they talked about their history and processes.

The staff is friendly and pretty casual.<//Text>< pictures>

< text>
The office moved to the first floor.  Suite 168.  The main entrance from the parking lot get you to the 2nd floor so, you will have to go downstairs via stairs or elevator.  There's always someone there to assist you when you enter the office.  They will ask you what you're here for and will give you a token.  I suggest getting there early in the morning or getting there after lunch time (around 1pm).  Otherwise, it can get busy here.  They do, however, come by to ask anyone who was just there to drop off the forms, which can make the waiting time shorter if you are just there to turn in the completed forms.    Thursdays are when orientations are usually held so, good luck finding the parking spot.</text>

<Rating>1<//Rating>< text>
My experience here was awful point blank. First off, their prices on their website don't match what they are at the club house. their twilight special is 30$ and that includes a cart. for 29$ you can go to dragonfly which is a far better course and far better maintained. I was expecting a lot more because the course conditions were just horrible. Their greens had numerous dead spots throughout the course and reminded me of airways 2.0. Then towards the end round, I was approached by an old man named randy who apparently worked at the course. He yelled at me and called me and called me a "Dumb F**k". He was yelling at me because apparently you aren't allowed to drive the carts anywhere but the cart paths. Most courses post signs when it is a cart path only day. The way i was approached was very disrespectful. for the price i recommend you using your money else where. its definitely not worth it. If i could give negative stars I would.</text>

<user_name>Keith Berry< /user_name>< review>
I have played Sherwood for almost twenty years. I love the course, but conditions are starting to deteriorate. Fairways are very long, and greens have lots of weeds in them. My biggest problem with Sherwood is how they treat junior golfers. My daughter plays for the local high school team. A few weeks ago she and a couple of her team mates were approached by Randy, the owner, and he asked them, "What are you doing here?" Not, "Hi, how are you ladies today?" "How are you playing?" No, he hassled them for being there. They are paying customers just like anyone else. Thank them for playing your course, don't hassle them. Finally, when I play with my ten year old son, they charge full price for both of us. About a month ago we played in front of my daughter and her team mates. Sherwood charged me $52 for myself and my ten year old to play nine holes with a cart. Absolutely ridiculous!! I'll be honest, if it wasn't so close to home, my family and I would play somewhere else. Stacey, if you read this, please, please, please, offer a reduced rate for juniors. Most courses have an NCGA "Youth on Course" rate of $5.</review>

<Review>This coffee shop is really cute. The decor is beautiful, food and coffee is tasty and the service is friendly and quick.

In the sense of ordering your coffee and food, this place is pretty traditional. You order your items at the counter and grab a number and a table (if you're dining in). The only bummer is that you have to pick up your coffee but it's not that big of a deal, I just wish I was made aware to pick up the coffee - especially since they give you a number. The food was delivered to the table though.

I ordered the Honey Latte which was BOMB! The Vanilla Latte was good too.

We also tried the Avocado Toast with Feta- it came on a thick slice of bread. I loved it. I thought it was hearty and healthy.

< text>
First time here; went through the drive thru, drive thru was small/short, so some people were backed up on the street. It was around 1230-1 when we went, the wait didn't take long, maybe a whole 3 mins. The people that took orders were nice, they were standing outside, kinda like how In and Out Burger/Chick-fil-A do it. I ordered the dragon smoothie, I was pleasantly surprised with the taste, very fresh, sweetened only with whatever was in the smothie, cold, and light and fruity tasting. They give paper straws here, so that was cool. Next time I come here I will try the lavender tea latte, iced, its probably really good. My bf had the hot coffee, best drink ever; I tried it and it was very good, I'm not a big coffee drinker either, but there was sugar and cream/milk in this one but it was light and you could taste the coffee, it wasn't overwhelmingly sweet. I saw some bad reviews of this place but honestly, my first time here and it was perfect service and our order was right, so maybe it was just a bad day for the other customers who complained about the customer service. I would highly recommend this place, there are a lot of options to choose from.<//text>

< Review>
Not at all impressed.  I don't know if I just had a one-off of not so great coffee but beyond that, the atmosphere is not that great, pricing is about 50% too high for the quality and the staff seems rather aloof.  So first off...the coffee.  I got the Bold blend and it tasted so watered down I wondered if it was Burger King or McDonalds coffee.  I sipped on it for a bit and then finally having to accept the fact that it was just terrible coffee, I chucked it into the garbage on my way into Target about 15 minutes later.  $3.50 in the trash can.  Oh well.  Live and learn. Literally, take the most average coffee you've ever had and cut it in half with water...that's what it tasted like.  Price....$3.50 for what was about a 16oz coffee?  This is why Panera exists.  You want good coffee?  Either go down the street to a place called Jennings House Cafe (no, I don't work there...their coffee is legit), Panera or Dunkin Donuts if you must.  This Better Buzz place is just completely overpriced.
Atmosphere...obnoxiously loud.  Staff banging on cookware and just generally not very welcoming and friendly.  Forget about trying to have a meeting of any kind there.  You'll be yelling across the table at your acquaintance due to the loud music, staff banging the cookware and just the overall loud ambiance of the place.  I guess I gave it two stars for whatever reason. Probably deserves one....if even.  Owners must be making an absolute killing at those prices.< /Review>
